colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.andrewlloydwebber.com">www<wbr />.andrewlloydwebber<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Andrew Lloyd Webber, Baron Lloyd-Webber</b> (born 22 March 1948)<sup id="cite_ref-whoswho_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> is an English <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">composer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Impresario" title="Impresario">impresario</a> of <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musical theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Several of his musicals have run for more than a decade both in the <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a> and on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a>. He has composed 13 musicals, a <a href="/wiki/Song_cycle" title="Song cycle">song cycle</a>, a set of <a href="/wiki/Variation_(music)" title="Variation (music)">variations</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">film scores</a>, and a Latin <a href="/wiki/Music_for_the_Requiem_Mass" title="Music for the Requiem Mass">Requiem Mass</a>. Several of his songs have been widely recorded and were hits outside of their parent musicals, notably "<a href="/wiki/The_Music_of_the_Night" title="The Music of the Night">The Music of the Night</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/All_I_Ask_of_You" title="All I Ask of You">All I Ask of You</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">The Phantom of the Opera</a></i>, "<a href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Know_How_to_Love_Him" title="I Don&#39;t Know How to Love Him">I Don\'t Know How to Love Him</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar" title="Jesus Christ Superstar">Jesus Christ Superstar</a></i>, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Cry_for_Me,_Argentina" class="mw-redirect" title="Don&#39;t Cry for Me, Argentina">Don\'t Cry for Me, Argentina</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(musical)" title="Evita (musical)">Evita</a></i>, "<a href="/wiki/Any_Dream_Will_Do_(song)" title="Any Dream Will Do (song)">Any Dream Will Do</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Joseph_and_the_Amazing_Technicolor_Dreamcoat" title="Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat">Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat</a></i> and "<a href="/wiki/Memory_(song)" title="Memory (song)">Memory</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">Cats</a></i>. In 2001 <i>The New York Times</i> referred to him as "the most commercially successful composer in history".<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Ranked the "fifth most powerful person in <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British culture</a>" by <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> in 2008, the lyricist <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a> stated "Andrew more or less single-handedly reinvented the musical."<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He has received a number of awards, including a <a href="/wiki/Knighthood" class="mw-redirect" title="Knighthood">knighthood</a> in 1992, followed by a <a href="/wiki/Peerage" title="Peerage">peerage</a> from Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> for services to Music, six <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tonys</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammys</a> (as well as the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Legend_Award" title="Grammy Legend Award">Grammy Legend Award</a>), an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>, fourteen <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivor Novello Award">Ivor Novello Awards</a>, seven <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Laurence Olivier Awards">Olivier Awards</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Award</a>, the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a>, and the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Classic_Brit_Awards" title="Classic Brit Awards">Classic Brit Award</a> for Outstanding Contribution to Music.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He has a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>, is an inductee into the <a href="/wiki/Songwriter%27s_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Songwriter&#39;s Hall of Fame">Songwriter\'s Hall of Fame</a>, and is a fellow of the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" class="mw-redirect" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He is one of only fifteen people to have won an <a href="/wiki/EGOT" class="mw-redirect" title="EGOT">Emmy, Oscar, Grammy and Tony</a>.\n</p><p>His company, the <a href="/wiki/Really_Useful_Group" title="Really Useful Group">Really Useful Group</a>, is one of the largest theatre operators in London. Producers in several parts of the UK have staged productions, including national tours, of the Lloyd Webber musicals under licence from the Really Useful Group. Lloyd Webber is also the president of the <a href="/wiki/Arts_Educational_Schools_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Arts Educational Schools London">Arts Educational Schools London</a>, a performing arts school located in Chiswick, West London. He is involved in a number of charitable activities, including the <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation">Elton John AIDS Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordoff-Robbins_music_therapy#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordoff-Robbins music therapy">Nordoff Robbins</a>, Prostate Cancer UK and <a href="/wiki/War_Child_(charity)" title="War Child (charity)">War Child</a>. In 1992 he set up the Andrew Lloyd Webber Foundation which supports the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">arts, culture and heritage in the UK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Early_life"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Early life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Professional_career"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Professional career</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Early_years"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Early years</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Mid-1970s"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Mid-1970s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#1980s"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">1980s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#1990s"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">1990s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#2000s"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">2000s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#2010s"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext">2010s</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Accusations_of_plagiarism"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Accusations of plagiarism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Honours_and_styles_of_address"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Honours and styles of address</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Honours"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Honours</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Styles_of_address"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Styles of address</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Awards"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Awards</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Academy_Awards"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Academy Awards</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Golden_Globes"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Golden Globes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Emmy_Awards"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Emmy Awards</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Grammy_Awards"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Grammy Awards</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Tony_Awards"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Tony Awards</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Olivier_Awards"><span class="tocnumber">6.6</span> <span class="toctext">Olivier Awards</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Other_awards"><span class="tocnumber">6.7</span> <span class="toctext">Other awards</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Shows"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Shows</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Film_adaptations"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Film adaptations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Other_works"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Other works</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Discography"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Discography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_School_Arch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Westminster_School_Arch.jpg/200px-Westminster_School_Arch.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Westminster_School_Arch.jpg/300px-Westminster_School_Arch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Westminster_School_Arch.jpg/400px-Westminster_School_Arch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_School_Arch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Westminster School</div></div></div>\n<p>Andrew Lloyd Webber was born in <a href="/wiki/Kensington" title="Kensington">Kensington</a>, London, the elder son of <a href="/wiki/William_Lloyd_Webber" title="William Lloyd Webber">William Lloyd Webber</a> (1914\xe2\x80\x931982), a composer and organist, and Jean Hermione Johnstone (1921\xe2\x80\x931993), a violinist and pianist.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> His younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Julian_Lloyd_Webber" title="Julian Lloyd Webber">Julian Lloyd Webber</a>, has had a notable career as a solo cellist.\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber started writing his own music at a young age, a <a href="/wiki/Suite_(music)" title="Suite (music)">suite</a> of six pieces at the age of nine. He also put on "productions" with Julian and his Aunt Viola in his toy theatre (which he built at Viola\'s suggestion). His aunt Viola, an actress, took him to see many of her shows and through the stage door into the world of the theatre. He also had originally set music to <i><a href="/wiki/Old_Possum%27s_Book_of_Practical_Cats" title="Old Possum&#39;s Book of Practical Cats">Old Possum\'s Book of Practical Cats</a></i> at the age of 15.\n</p><p>In 1965, Lloyd Webber was a <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Scholar" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Scholar">Queen\'s Scholar</a> at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_School" title="Westminster School">Westminster School</a> and studied history for a term at <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_College,_Oxford" title="Magdalen College, Oxford">Magdalen College, Oxford</a>, although he abandoned the course in the winter of 1965 to study at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Music" title="Royal College of Music">Royal College of Music</a> and pursue his interest in <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musical theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_career">Professional career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Professional career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1965, when Lloyd Webber was a 17-year-old budding musical-theatre composer, he was introduced to the 20-year-old aspiring pop-song writer <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chandler_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chandler-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ellis_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ellis-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Their first collaboration was <i><a href="/wiki/The_Likes_of_Us" title="The Likes of Us">The Likes of Us</a></i>, a musical based on the true story of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_John_Barnardo" title="Thomas John Barnardo">Thomas John Barnardo</a>. They produced a demo tape of that work in 1966,<sup id="cite_ref-chandler_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chandler-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> but the project failed to gain a backer.<sup id="cite_ref-ellis_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ellis-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although composed in 1965, <i>The Likes of Us</i> was not publicly performed until 2005, when a production was staged at Lloyd Webber\'s <a href="/wiki/Sydmonton_Festival" title="Sydmonton Festival">Sydmonton Festival</a>. In 2008, amateur rights were released by the National Operatic and Dramatic Association (NODA) in association with the Really Useful Group. The first amateur performance was by a children\'s theatre group in Cornwall called "Kidz R Us". Stylistically, <i>The Likes of Us</i> is fashioned after the Broadway musical of the 1940s and 1950s; it opens with a traditional overture comprising a medley of tunes from the show, and the score reflects some of Lloyd Webber\'s early influences, particularly <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rodgers" title="Richard Rodgers">Richard Rodgers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Loewe" title="Frederick Loewe">Frederick Loewe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Bart" title="Lionel Bart">Lionel Bart</a>. In this respect, it is markedly different from the composer\'s later work, which tends to be either predominantly or wholly <a href="/wiki/Through-composed" title="Through-composed">through-composed</a>, and closer in form to opera than to the Broadway musical.\n</p><p>In the summer of 1967 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alan_Doggett&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alan Doggett (page does not exist)">Alan Doggett</a>, a family friend of the Lloyd Webbers who had assisted on <i>The Likes of Us</i> and who was the music teacher at the <a href="/wiki/Colet_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Colet Court">Colet Court</a> school in London, commissioned Lloyd Webber and Rice to write a piece for the school\'s choir.<sup id="cite_ref-chandler_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chandler-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ellis_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ellis-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Doggett requested a "pop cantata" along the lines of <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Chappell" title="Herbert Chappell">Herbert Chappell</a>\'s <i>The Daniel Jazz</i> (1963) and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Hurd_(composer)" title="Michael Hurd (composer)">Michael Hurd</a>\'s <i>Jonah-Man Jazz</i> (1966), both of which had been published by <a href="/wiki/Novello_%26_Co" class="mw-redirect" title="Novello &amp; Co">Novello</a> and were based on the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chandler_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chandler-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The request for the new piece came with a 100-<a href="/wiki/Guinea_(coin)" title="Guinea (coin)">guinea</a> advance from Novello.<sup id="cite_ref-chandler_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chandler-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> This resulted in <i><a href="/wiki/Joseph_and_the_Amazing_Technicolor_Dreamcoat" title="Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat">Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat</a></i>, a retelling of the biblical story of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_(son_of_Jacob)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph (son of Jacob)">Joseph</a>, in which Lloyd Webber and Rice humorously pastiched a number of pop-music styles such as Elvis-style rock\'n\'roll, <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">Calypso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country music</a>. <i>Joseph</i> began life as a short <a href="/wiki/Cantata" title="Cantata">cantata</a> that gained some recognition on its second staging with a favourable review in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>. For its subsequent performances, Rice and Lloyd Webber revised the show and added new songs to expand it to a more substantial length. Continued expansion eventually culminated in a 1972 stage musical and then a two-hour-long production being staged in the West End in 1973 on the back of the success of <i>Jesus Christ Superstar</i>.\n</p><p>In 1969 Rice and Lloyd Webber wrote a song for the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> called "Try It and See", which was not selected. With rewritten lyrics it became "King Herod\'s Song" in their third musical, <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar" title="Jesus Christ Superstar">Jesus Christ Superstar</a></i> (1970).\n</p><p>The planned follow-up to <i>Jesus Christ Superstar</i> was a musical comedy based on the <a href="/wiki/Jeeves_and_Wooster" title="Jeeves and Wooster">Jeeves and Wooster</a> novels by <a href="/wiki/P._G._Wodehouse" title="P. G. Wodehouse">P. G. Wodehouse</a>. Tim Rice was uncertain about this venture, partly because of his concern that he might not be able to do justice to the novels that he and Lloyd Webber so admired.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After doing some initial work on the lyrics, he pulled out of the project<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2018)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and Lloyd Webber subsequently wrote the musical <i>Jeeves</i> with <a href="/wiki/Alan_Ayckbourn" title="Alan Ayckbourn">Alan Ayckbourn</a>, who provided the book and lyrics. <i>Jeeves</i> failed to make any impact at the box office and closed after a run of only three weeks in 1975.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Many years later, Lloyd Webber and Ayckbourn revisited this project, producing a thoroughly reworked and more successful version entitled <i><a href="/wiki/By_Jeeves" title="By Jeeves">By Jeeves</a></i> (1996). Only two of the songs from the original production remained ("Half a Moment" and "Banjo Boy").<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-1970s">Mid-1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mid-1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lloyd Webber collaborated with Rice once again to write <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(musical)" title="Evita (musical)">Evita</a></i> (1978 in London/1979 in U.S.), a musical based on the life of <a href="/wiki/Eva_Per%C3%B3n" title="Eva Per\xc3\xb3n">Eva Per\xc3\xb3n</a>. As with <i>Jesus Christ Superstar</i>, Evita was released first as a concept album (1976) and featured <a href="/wiki/Julie_Covington" title="Julie Covington">Julie Covington</a> singing the part of Eva Per\xc3\xb3n. The song "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Cry_for_Me_Argentina" title="Don&#39;t Cry for Me Argentina">Don\'t Cry for Me Argentina</a>" became a hit single and the musical was staged at the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Theatre" title="Prince Edward Theatre">Prince Edward Theatre</a> in a production directed by <a href="/wiki/Harold_Prince" title="Harold Prince">Harold Prince</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Elaine_Paige" title="Elaine Paige">Elaine Paige</a> in the title role.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Patti_LuPone" title="Patti LuPone">Patti LuPone</a> created the role of Eva on Broadway for which she won a Tony.  <i>Evita</i> was a highly successful show that ran for ten years in the West End. It transferred to Broadway in 1979. Rice and Lloyd Webber parted ways soon after <i>Evita</i>. In an interview in 2011, LuPone commented, "He writes crap music... <i>Evita</i> was his best score, <i>Evita</i> in its bizarreness - when I first heard it I thought \'I swear to God, he hated women\' [...] There are some very romantic moments in his music, and there is some real...trash that he doesn\'t even think about parting with. He\'s not a very good editor of his own stuff."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1978, Lloyd Webber embarked on a solo project, the <i><a href="/wiki/Variations_(Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_album)" title="Variations (Andrew Lloyd Webber album)">Variations</a></i>, with his cellist brother <a href="/wiki/Julian_Lloyd_Webber" title="Julian Lloyd Webber">Julian</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Caprice_No._24_(Paganini)" title="Caprice No. 24 (Paganini)">24th Caprice by Paganini</a>, which reached number two in the pop album chart in the United Kingdom. The main theme was used as the theme tune for <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>\'s long-running <i><a href="/wiki/South_Bank_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="South Bank Show">South Bank Show</a></i> throughout its 32-year run. The same year, Lloyd Webber also composed a new theme tune for the long-running documentary series <i><a href="/wiki/Whicker%27s_World" title="Whicker&#39;s World">Whicker\'s World</a></i>, which was used from 1978 to 1980.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lloyd Webber was the subject of <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Your_Life_(UK_TV_series)" title="This Is Your Life (UK TV series)">This Is Your Life</a></i> in November 1980 when he was surprised by <a href="/wiki/Eamonn_Andrews" title="Eamonn Andrews">Eamonn Andrews</a> in the foyer of Thames Television\'s Euston Road Studios. He would be honoured a second time by the television programme in November 1994 when <a href="/wiki/Michael_Aspel" title="Michael Aspel">Michael Aspel</a> surprised him at the <a href="/wiki/Adelphi_Theatre" title="Adelphi Theatre">Adelphi Theatre</a>.\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber embarked on his next project without a lyricist, turning instead to the poetry of <a href="/wiki/T._S._Eliot" title="T. S. Eliot">T. S. Eliot</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">Cats</a></i> (1981) was to become the longest running musical in London, where it ran for 21 years before closing. On Broadway, <i>Cats</i> ran for 18 years, a record which would ultimately be broken by another Lloyd Webber musical, <i>The Phantom of the Opera</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BroadwayLength_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BroadwayLength-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Starlight_Express" title="Starlight Express">Starlight Express</a></i> (1984) was a commercial hit, but received negative reviews from the critics. It enjoyed a record run in the West End, but ran for less than two years on Broadway. The show has also seen two tours of the US, as well as an Australian/Japanese production, a three-year UK touring production, which transferred to New Zealand later in 2009. The show also runs full-time in a custom-built theatre in <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a>, Germany, where it has been running since 1988.\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber wrote a <a href="/wiki/Requiem_Mass" class="mw-redirect" title="Requiem Mass">Requiem Mass</a> dedicated to his father, William, who had died in 1982. It premiered at St. Thomas Church in New York on 24 February 1985. Church music had been a part of the composer\'s upbringing and the composition was inspired by an article he had read about the plight of Cambodian orphans. Lloyd Webber had on a number of occasions written sacred music for the annual <a href="/wiki/Sydmonton_Festival" title="Sydmonton Festival">Sydmonton Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Lloyd Webber received a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> in 1986 for <i>Requiem</i> in the category of best classical composition. <i><a href="/wiki/Pie_Jesu" title="Pie Jesu">Pie Jesu</a></i> from Requiem achieved a high placing on the UK pop charts. Perhaps because of its large orchestration, live performances of the Requiem are rare.\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Cricket_(musical)" title="Cricket (musical)">Cricket</a></i> (1986), also called <i>Cricket (Hearts and Wickets)</i>, reunited Lloyd Webber with Tim Rice to create this short musical for <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth</a>\'s 60th birthday, first performed at <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a>. Several of the tunes were later used for <i>Aspects of Love</i> and <i>Sunset Boulevard</i>.\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber also premiered <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">The Phantom of the Opera</a></i> in 1986, inspired by the <a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera" title="The Phantom of the Opera">1911 Gaston Leroux novel</a>. He wrote the part of Christine for his then-wife, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Brightman" title="Sarah Brightman">Sarah Brightman</a>, who played the role in the original London and Broadway productions alongside <a href="/wiki/Michael_Crawford" title="Michael Crawford">Michael Crawford</a> as the Phantom. The production was directed by Harold Prince, who had also earlier directed <i>Evita.</i> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Hart_(lyricist)" title="Charles Hart (lyricist)">Charles Hart</a> wrote the lyrics for <i>Phantom</i> with some additional material provided by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stilgoe" title="Richard Stilgoe">Richard Stilgoe</a>, with whom Lloyd Webber co-wrote the book of the musical. It became a hit and is still running in both the West End and on Broadway; in January 2006 it overtook <i>Cats</i> as the longest-running musical on Broadway. On 11 February 2012, <i>Phantom of the Opera</i> played its 10,000th show on Broadway.<sup id="cite_ref-BroadwayLength_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BroadwayLength-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Aspects_of_Love" title="Aspects of Love">Aspects of Love</a></i> followed in 1989, a musical based on the story by <a href="/wiki/David_Garnett" title="David Garnett">David Garnett</a>. The lyrics were by <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a> and Charles Hart and the original production was directed by Trevor Nunn. <i>Aspects</i> had a run of four years in London, but closed after less than a year on Broadway. It has since gone on a tour of the UK.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lloyd Webber was asked to write a song for the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Barcelona Olympics</a> and composed "<a href="/wiki/Amigos_Para_Siempre" title="Amigos Para Siempre">Amigos Para Siempre</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 Friends for Life" with Don Black providing the lyrics. This song was performed by <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Brightman" title="Sarah Brightman">Sarah Brightman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carreras" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Carreras">Jos\xc3\xa9 Carreras</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Los_Angeles_(California,_USA),_Hollywood_Boulevard,_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Los_Angeles_%28California%2C_USA%29%2C_Hollywood_Boulevard%2C_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg/220px-Los_Angeles_%28California%2C_USA%29%2C_Hollywood_Boulevard%2C_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Los_Angeles_%28California%2C_USA%29%2C_Hollywood_Boulevard%2C_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg/330px-Los_Angeles_%28California%2C_USA%29%2C_Hollywood_Boulevard%2C_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Los_Angeles_%28California%2C_USA%29%2C_Hollywood_Boulevard%2C_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg/440px-Los_Angeles_%28California%2C_USA%29%2C_Hollywood_Boulevard%2C_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3524" data-file-height="3137" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Los_Angeles_(California,_USA),_Hollywood_Boulevard,_Sir_Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_--_2012_--_4980.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloyd Webber was awarded a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> in 1993 for his contribution to live theatre</div></div></div>\n<p>Lloyd Webber had toyed with the idea of writing a musical based on <a href="/wiki/Billy_Wilder" title="Billy Wilder">Billy Wilder</a>\'s critically acclaimed movie, <i><a href="/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard_(1950_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunset Boulevard (1950 film)">Sunset Boulevard</a></i>, since the early 1970s when he saw the film, but the project didn\'t come to fruition until after the completion of <i>Aspects of Love</i> when the composer finally managed to secure the rights from <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The composer worked with two collaborators, as he had done on <i>Aspects of Love</i>; this time Christopher Hampton and <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a> shared equal credit for the book and lyrics. The show opened at the <a href="/wiki/Adelphi_Theatre" title="Adelphi Theatre">Adelphi Theatre</a> in London on 12 July 1993, and ran for 1,529 performances. In spite of the show\'s popularity and extensive run in London\'s West End, it lost money due to the sheer expense of the production.\n</p><p>In 1994, <i>Sunset Boulevard</i> became a successful Broadway show, opening with the largest advance in Broadway history, and winning seven Tony Awards that year. Even so, by its closing in 1997, "it had not recouped its reported $13&#160;million investment."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\nFrom 1995-2000, Lloyd Webber wrote the Matters of Taste column in The Daily Telegraph where he reviewed restaurants and hotels, and these were illustrated by Lucinda Rogers.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1998, Lloyd Webber released a film version of <i>Cats</i>, which was filmed at the Adelphi Theatre in London. David Mallet directed the film, and Gillian Lynne choreographed it. The cast consisted of performers who had been in the show before, including Ken Page (the original Old Deuteronomy on Broadway), Elaine Paige (original Grizabella in London) and Sir John Mills as Gus: the Theatre Cat.\n</p><p>In 1998 <i><a href="/wiki/Whistle_Down_the_Wind_(1996_musical)" title="Whistle Down the Wind (1996 musical)">Whistle Down the Wind</a></i> made its debut, a musical written with lyrics supplied by Jim Steinman. Originally opening in Washington, Lloyd Webber was reportedly not happy with the casting or Harold Prince\'s production and the show was subsequently revised for a London staging directed by Gale Edwards. The production included the <a href="/wiki/Boyzone" title="Boyzone">Boyzone</a> number-one hit "No Matter What", which only left the UK charts when the price of the CD single was changed to drop it out of the official top ten. His <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beautiful_Game_(musical)" title="The Beautiful Game (musical)">The Beautiful Game</a></i> opened in London and has never been seen on Broadway. The show had a respectable run at The Cambridge Theatre in London. The show has been re-worked into a new musical, <i>The Boys in the Photograph</i>, which had its world premi\xc3\xa8re at <a href="/wiki/The_Liverpool_Institute_for_Performing_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="The Liverpool Institute for Performing Arts">The Liverpool Institute for Performing Arts</a> in April 2008.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Having achieved great popular success in musical theatre, Lloyd Webber was referred to by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> in 2001 as "the most commercially successful composer in history."<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002 he turned producer, bringing the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Bombay_Dreams" title="Bombay Dreams">Bombay Dreams</a></i> to London. With music by <a href="/wiki/Indian_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Music">Indian Music</a> composer <a href="/wiki/A.R._Rahman" class="mw-redirect" title="A.R. Rahman">A.R. Rahman</a> and lyrics by Don Black, it ran for two years at the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Victoria_Theatre" title="Apollo Victoria Theatre">Apollo Victoria Theatre</a>. A revised Broadway production at the <a href="/wiki/Broadway_Theatre_(53rd_Street)" title="Broadway Theatre (53rd Street)">Broadway Theatre</a> two years later ran for only 284 performances.\n</p><p>On 16 September 2004, his production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woman_in_White_(musical)" title="The Woman in White (musical)">The Woman in White</a></i> opened at the Palace Theatre in London. It ran for 19 months and 500 performances. A revised production opened on Broadway at the Marquis Theatre on 17 November 2005. Garnering mixed reviews from critics, due in part to the frequent absences of the show\'s star Maria Friedman due to breast cancer treatment, it closed only a brief three months later on 19 February 2006.\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber produced a staging of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music" title="The Sound of Music">The Sound of Music</a></i>, which d\xc3\xa9buted November 2006. He made the controversial decision to choose an unknown to play leading lady Maria, who was found through the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s reality television show <i><a href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Solve_a_Problem_like_Maria%3F" title="How Do You Solve a Problem like Maria?">How Do You Solve a Problem like Maria?</a></i>, in which he was a judge.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The winner of the show was <a href="/wiki/Connie_Fisher" title="Connie Fisher">Connie Fisher</a>.\n</p><p>It was announced on 25 August 2006, on his personal website, that his next project would be <i><a href="/wiki/The_Master_and_Margarita" title="The Master and Margarita">The Master and Margarita</a></i>; however, it was announced in late March 2007 that he had abandoned the project.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg/330px-2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg" width="330" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg/495px-2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg/660px-2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2036" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2006_Kennedy_Center_honorees.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and First Lady <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura Bush</a> stand with the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Kennedy Center">Kennedy Center</a> honourees in the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Room_(White_House)" title="Blue Room (White House)">Blue Room</a> of the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> during a reception Sunday, 3 December 2006. From left, they are: singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/William_%22Smokey%22_Robinson" class="mw-redirect" title="William &quot;Smokey&quot; Robinson">William "Smokey" Robinson</a>; Andrew Lloyd Webber; country singer <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>; film director <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>; and conductor <a href="/wiki/Zubin_Mehta" title="Zubin Mehta">Zubin Mehta</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In September 2006, Lloyd Webber was named to be a recipient of the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a> with <a href="/wiki/Zubin_Mehta" title="Zubin Mehta">Zubin Mehta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Robinson" title="Smokey Robinson">Smokey Robinson</a>. He was recognised for his outstanding contribution to American performing arts.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He attended the ceremony on 3 December 2006; it aired on 26 December 2006. On 11 February 2007, Lloyd Webber was featured as a guest judge on the reality television show <i><a href="/wiki/Grease:_You%27re_the_One_that_I_Want!" class="mw-redirect" title="Grease: You&#39;re the One that I Want!">Grease: You\'re the One that I Want!</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The contestants all sang "The Phantom of the Opera".\n</p><p>Between April and June 2007, he appeared in BBC One\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Any_Dream_Will_Do_(TV_series)" title="Any Dream Will Do (TV series)">Any Dream Will Do!</a></i>, which followed the same format as <i><a href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Solve_a_Problem_Like_Maria%3F" class="mw-redirect" title="How Do You Solve a Problem Like Maria?">How Do You Solve a Problem Like Maria?</a></i>. Its aim was to find a new Joseph for his revival of <i><a href="/wiki/Joseph_and_the_Amazing_Technicolor_Dreamcoat" title="Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat">Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Lee_Mead" title="Lee Mead">Lee Mead</a> won the contest after quitting his part in the ensemble \xe2\x80\x93 and as understudy in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">The Phantom of the Opera</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 to compete for the role. Viewers\' telephone voting during the series raised more than <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>500,000 for the BBC\'s annual <i><a href="/wiki/Children_in_Need" title="Children in Need">Children in Need</a></i> charity appeal, according to host Graham Norton on air during the final.\n</p><p>In 2007, Lloyd Webber\'s cat, Otto, leaped onto his <a href="/wiki/Clavinova" title="Clavinova">Clavinova</a> piano and "destroyed the entire score for the new \'Phantom\' in one fell swoop." The Phantom in question was The Phantom of Manhattan, a planned sequel to Phantom of the Opera.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 July 2007, Lloyd Webber presented excerpts from his musicals as part of the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Diana" title="Concert for Diana">Concert for Diana</a> held at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, London, an event organised to celebrate the life of <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Princess Diana</a> almost 10 years after her death.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">BBC Radio 2</a> broadcast a concert of music from the Lloyd Webber musicals on 24 August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Denise_Van_Outen" class="mw-redirect" title="Denise Van Outen">Denise Van Outen</a> introduced songs from <i><a href="/wiki/Whistle_Down_the_Wind_(1996_musical)" title="Whistle Down the Wind (1996 musical)">Whistle Down the Wind</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beautiful_Game_(musical)" title="The Beautiful Game (musical)">The Beautiful Game</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tell_Me_on_a_Sunday" title="Tell Me on a Sunday">Tell Me on a Sunday</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woman_in_White_(musical)" title="The Woman in White (musical)">The Woman in White</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(musical)" title="Evita (musical)">Evita</a></i>  and <i><a href="/wiki/Joseph_and_the_Amazing_Technicolor_Dreamcoat" title="Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat">Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 as well as Rodgers and Hammerstein\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music" title="The Sound of Music">The Sound of Music</a></i>, which Lloyd Webber revived in 2006 at the <a href="/wiki/London_Palladium" title="London Palladium">London Palladium</a>, and the 2002 musical <i><a href="/wiki/Bombay_Dreams" title="Bombay Dreams">Bombay Dreams</a></i>.\n</p><p>In April 2008, Lloyd Webber reprised his role as judge, this time in the BBC musical talent show <i><a href="/wiki/I%27d_Do_Anything_(BBC_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="I&#39;d Do Anything (BBC TV series)">I\'d Do Anything</a></i>. The show followed a similar format to its <i>Maria</i> and <i>Joseph</i> predecessors, this time involving a search for an actress to play the role of Nancy in an upcoming West End production of the <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Bart" title="Lionel Bart">Lionel Bart</a> musical <i><a href="/wiki/Oliver!" title="Oliver!">Oliver!</a></i> The show also featured a search for three young actors to play and share the title character\'s role, but the show\'s main focus was on the search for Nancy. The role was won by <a href="/wiki/Jodie_Prenger" title="Jodie Prenger">Jodie Prenger</a> despite Lloyd Webber\'s stated preference for one of the other contestants; the winners of the Oliver role were Harry Stott, Gwion Wyn-Jones and Laurence Jeffcoate. Also in April 2008. Lloyd Webber was featured on the U.S. talent show <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>, acting as a mentor when the 6 finalists had to select one of his songs to perform for the judges that week.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jadeandandrewe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Jadeandandrewe.jpg/220px-Jadeandandrewe.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Jadeandandrewe.jpg/330px-Jadeandandrewe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Jadeandandrewe.jpg/440px-Jadeandandrewe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3315" data-file-height="2210" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jadeandandrewe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloyd Webber and the UK\'s Eurovision entrant <a href="/wiki/Jade_Ewen" title="Jade Ewen">Jade Ewen</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-11-15_%D0%92%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD,_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80_(2).jpeg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2008-11-15_%D0%92%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%2C_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80_%282%29.jpeg/330px-2008-11-15_%D0%92%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%2C_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80_%282%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2008-11-15_%D0%92%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%2C_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80_%282%29.jpeg/440px-2008-11-15_%D0%92%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%2C_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80_%282%29.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="393" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-11-15_%D0%92%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD,_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80_(2).jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloyd Webber and Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> prior to the <a href="/wiki/2009_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Eurovision Song Contest">2009 Eurovision Song Contest</a> held in Moscow</div></div></div>\n<p>Lloyd Webber accepted the challenge of managing the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2009" title="United Kingdom in the Eurovision Song Contest 2009">UK\'s entry</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2009_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Eurovision Song Contest">2009 Eurovision Song Contest</a>, to be held in Moscow. In early 2009 a series, called <i><a href="/wiki/Eurovision:_Your_Country_Needs_You" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurovision: Your Country Needs You">Eurovision: Your Country Needs You</a></i>, was broadcast to find a performer for a song that he would compose for the competition. <a href="/wiki/Jade_Ewen" title="Jade Ewen">Jade Ewen</a> won the right to represent Britain, winning with <a href="/wiki/It%27s_My_Time_(Eurovision_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="It&#39;s My Time (Eurovision song)">It\'s My Time</a>, by Lloyd Webber and <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a>. At the contest, Lloyd Webber accompanied her on the piano during the performance. The United Kingdom finished 5th in the contest. The winner was <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Rybak" title="Alexander Rybak">Alexander Rybak</a> with his composition "<a href="/wiki/Fairytale_(Alexander_Rybak_song)" title="Fairytale (Alexander Rybak song)">Fairytale</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 October 2009, Lloyd Webber launched the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Never_Dies_(musical)" title="Love Never Dies (musical)">Love Never Dies</a></i> at a press conference held at <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Theatre" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Theatre">Her Majesty\'s Theatre</a>, where the original <i>Phantom</i> has been running since 1986. Also present were <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Boggess" title="Sierra Boggess">Sierra Boggess</a>, who had been cast as <a href="/wiki/Christine_Daa%C3%A9" title="Christine Daa\xc3\xa9">Christine Daa\xc3\xa9</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ramin_Karimloo" title="Ramin Karimloo">Ramin Karimloo</a>, who portrayed <a href="/wiki/Erik_(The_Phantom_of_the_Opera)" title="Erik (The Phantom of the Opera)">Phantom</a>, a role he had recently played in the West End.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the opening of <i>Love Never Dies</i>, Lloyd Webber again began a search for a new musical theatre performer in the BBC One series <i><a href="/wiki/Over_the_Rainbow_(2010_TV_series)" title="Over the Rainbow (2010 TV series)">Over the Rainbow</a></i>. He cast the winner, <a href="/wiki/Danielle_Hope" title="Danielle Hope">Danielle Hope</a>, in the role of <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Gale" title="Dorothy Gale">Dorothy</a>, and a dog to play <a href="/wiki/Toto_(Oz)" title="Toto (Oz)">Toto</a> in his forthcoming stage production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_(2011_musical)" title="The Wizard of Oz (2011 musical)">The Wizard of Oz</a></i>. He and lyricist and composer <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a> wrote a number of new songs for the production to supplement the songs from the film.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 March 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_(2011_musical)" title="The Wizard of Oz (2011 musical)">The Wizard of Oz</a></i> opened at The Palladium Theatre, starring Danielle Hope as Dorothy and Michael Crawford as the Wizard.\n</p><p>In 2012 Lloyd Webber fronted a new <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> primetime show <i><a href="/wiki/Superstar_(UK_TV_series)" title="Superstar (UK TV series)">Superstar</a></i> which gave the UK public the chance to decide who would play the starring role of Jesus in an upcoming arena tour of <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar" title="Jesus Christ Superstar">Jesus Christ Superstar</a></i>. The arena tour started in September 2012 and also starred comedian <a href="/wiki/Tim_Minchin" title="Tim Minchin">Tim Minchin</a> as Judas Iscariot, former Spice Girl <a href="/wiki/Melanie_C" title="Melanie C">Melanie C</a> as Mary Magdalene and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a> DJ <a href="/wiki/Chris_Moyles" title="Chris Moyles">Chris Moyles</a> as King Herod.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Tickets for most venues went on sale on 18 May 2012.\n</p><p>Webber caused controversy with a series of comments about Eurovision in a <i>Radio Times</i> interview.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> He said: "I don\'t think there\'s any point in beating around the bush. I saw no black faces on the programme <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2012">Eurovision 2012</a>. I was questioned by the press over Jade Ewen\'s race, and I think we would have placed second, but there is a problem when you go further east. If you\'re talking about Western Europe it\'s fine, but Ukraine, not so good."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The EBU corrected Webber, telling him Ukraine\'s singer <a href="/wiki/Gaitana_(singer)" title="Gaitana (singer)">Gaitana</a> was black, that year\'s winner <a href="/wiki/Loreen_(singer)" title="Loreen (singer)">Loreen</a> for Sweden was of North African background and accompanied by a black backing dancer, and France\'s contestant <a href="/wiki/Anggun" title="Anggun">Anggun</a> was Indonesian. The contest organisers also told Webber that black singer <a href="/wiki/Dave_Benton" title="Dave Benton">Dave Benton</a> won for Estonia in 2001. The EBU thoroughly denied racism in its show, and insisted it unites Europe for three nights in a year.\n</p><p>In 2013, Webber reunited with <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Hampton" title="Christopher Hampton">Christopher Hampton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Ward_the_Musical" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Ward the Musical">Stephen Ward the Musical</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, it was announced that Webber\'s next project would be a <a href="/wiki/School_of_Rock_(musical)" title="School of Rock (musical)">musical</a> adaptation of the 2003 film <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Rock" title="School of Rock">School of Rock</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On 19 January 2015 auditions opened for children aged nine to fifteen in cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Rock_(company)" title="School of Rock (company)">School of Rock</a> music education program, which predated the film by several years.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MusicalAuditions_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MusicalAuditions-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber\'s memoir, <i>Unmasked</i>, was published in March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT18_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT18-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 9, 2018 Webber, along with Tim Rice and <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a> each won a Emmy for <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar_Live_in_Concert" title="Jesus Christ Superstar Live in Concert">Jesus Christ Superstar Live in Concert</a>. With this win, Webber, Rice and Legend joined the <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_won_Academy,_Emmy,_Grammy,_and_Tony_Awards" title="List of people who have won Academy, Emmy, Grammy, and Tony Awards">list of people who have won Academy, Emmy, Grammy, and Tony Awards</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accusations_of_plagiarism">Accusations of plagiarism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Accusations of plagiarism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Lloyd Webber has been accused of plagiarism in his works. The Dutch composer <a href="/wiki/Louis_Andriessen" title="Louis Andriessen">Louis Andriessen</a> commented that: "Andrew Lloyd Webber has yet to think up a single note; in fact, the poor guy\'s never invented one note by himself. That\'s rather poor".<sup id="cite_ref-Moutby_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moutby-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber\'s biographer, John Snelson, countered such accusations. He acknowledged a similarity between the Andante movement of <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_(Mendelssohn)" title="Violin Concerto (Mendelssohn)">Mendelssohn\'s Violin Concerto in E minor</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar" title="Jesus Christ Superstar">Jesus Christ Superstar</a></i> song "<a href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Know_How_to_Love_Him" title="I Don&#39;t Know How to Love Him">I Don\'t Know How to Love Him</a>", but wrote that Lloyd Webber:\n</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>...brings a new dramatic tension to Mendelssohn\'s original melody through the confused emotions of Mary Magdalene. The opening theme may be Mendelssohn, but the rhythmic and harmonic treatment along with new lines of highly effective melodic development are Lloyd Webber\'s. The song works in its own right as its many performers and audiences can witness.<sup id="cite_ref-Moutby_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moutby-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The songwriter <a href="/wiki/Ray_Repp" title="Ray Repp">Ray Repp</a> claimed in a court case that Lloyd Webber had stolen a melody from his own song "Till You", but the court ruled in Lloyd Webber\'s favour.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was another accusation of plagiarism regarding <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>. The band released their sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Meddle" title="Meddle">Meddle</a></i> in 1971, and the sixth track of the album "<a href="/wiki/Echoes_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="Echoes (Pink Floyd song)">Echoes</a>" had a riff which Lloyd Webber based his "iconic" organ riff from <i>Phantom of the opera</i>. Very similar notes were taken, same time signature of 12/8, along with the order of the notes played. Lloyd Webber\'s pipe organ riff from the opera played: D, C#, C, B, A#, then ascending A#, B, C, C#, D. Pink Floyd\'s "Echoes" plays: C#, C, B, A#, A, then ascending A, A#, B, C, C#. Pink Floyd bassist <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a> pointed this out, but said he does not care to take it to court. "It probably is actionable. It really is! But I think that life\'s too long to bother with suing Andrew fucking Lloyd Webber."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-11-15_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/2008-11-15_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80.jpeg/180px-2008-11-15_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80.jpeg" width="180" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/2008-11-15_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80.jpeg/270px-2008-11-15_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/2008-11-15_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-11-15_%D0%AD%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D1%8E_%D0%9B%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%B4_%D0%A3%D1%8D%D0%B1%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloyd Webber in 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>Lloyd Webber has been married three times. He married first Sarah Hugill on 24 July 1971 and they divorced on 14 November 1983. Together they had two children: a daughter and a son:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Imogen_Lloyd_Webber" title="Imogen Lloyd Webber">Imogen Lloyd Webber</a> (born 31 March 1977)</li>\n<li>Nicholas Lloyd Webber (born 2 July 1979)</li></ul>\n<p>He then married singer <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Brightman" title="Sarah Brightman">Sarah Brightman</a> on 22 March 1984 in <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>. He cast Brightman in the lead role in his musical <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">The Phantom of the Opera</a></i>, among other notable roles. They divorced on 3 January 1990.\n</p><p>Thirdly, he married <a href="/wiki/Madeleine_Gurdon" title="Madeleine Gurdon">Madeleine Gurdon</a> in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Westminster" class="mw-redirect" title="London Borough of Westminster">Westminster</a> on 9 February 1991. They have three children, two sons and one daughter, all of whom were born in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Westminster" class="mw-redirect" title="London Borough of Westminster">Westminster</a>:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Alastair Adam Lloyd Webber (born 3 May 1992)</li>\n<li>William Richard Lloyd Webber (born 24 August 1993)</li>\n<li>Isabella Aurora Lloyd Webber (born 30 April 1996).</li></ul>\n<p>Lloyd Webber and his third wife Madeleine founded the Watership Down Stud in 1992.  In 1996, they expanded their equestrian holdings by purchasing Kiltinan Castle Stud near <a href="/wiki/Fethard,_County_Tipperary" title="Fethard, County Tipperary">Fethard in County Tipperary, Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday Times Rich List 2006">Sunday Times Rich List 2006</a></i> ranked him the 87th-richest man in Britain with an estimated fortune of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>700&#160;million. His wealth increased to \xc2\xa3750&#160;million in 2007, but the publication ranked him <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List_2008" title="Sunday Times Rich List 2008">101st in 2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He lives at <a href="/wiki/Sydmonton_Court" title="Sydmonton Court">Sydmonton Court</a>, Hampshire, and owns much of nearby <a href="/wiki/Watership_Down,_Hampshire" title="Watership Down, Hampshire">Watership Down</a>.\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber is an <a href="/wiki/Art_collector" class="mw-redirect" title="Art collector">art collector</a>, with a passion for <a href="/wiki/Victorian_painting" title="Victorian painting">Victorian painting</a>. An exhibition of works from his collection was presented at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Academy">Royal Academy</a> in 2003 under the title <i>Pre-Raphaelite and Other Masters \xe2\x80\x93 The Andrew Lloyd Webber Collection</i>. In 2006, Lloyd Webber planned to sell <i><a href="/wiki/Portrait_of_Angel_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Soto" title="Portrait of Angel Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Soto">Portrait of Angel Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Soto</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a> to benefit the Andrew Lloyd Webber Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In November 2006, he withdrew the painting from auction after a claim that the previous owner had been forced to sell it under duress in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> An out-of-court settlement was reached, where the foundation retained ownership rights.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On 23 June 2010, the painting was sold at auction for \xc2\xa334.7&#160;million to an anonymous telephone bidder.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lloyd Webber was made a <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/Life_peer" title="Life peer">life peer</a> in 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-gaz_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaz-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> however by the end of 2015, he had voted only 33 times.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Politically, Lloyd Webber has supported the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>, allowing his song "<a href="/wiki/Take_That_Look_Off_Your_Face" title="Take That Look Off Your Face">Take That Look Off Your Face</a>" to be used on a party promotional film seen by an estimated 1 million people before the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2005" title="United Kingdom general election, 2005">2005 general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, he publicly criticised the Labour government\'s introduction of a new 50% rate of income tax on Britain\'s top earners, claiming it would damage the country by encouraging talented people to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In August 2014, Lloyd Webber was one of 200 public figures who were signatories to a letter to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> opposing <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">Scottish independence</a> in the run-up to September\'s <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">referendum on that issue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\nIn October 2015 Lloyd Webber was involved in a controversial House of Lords vote over proposed cuts to <a href="/wiki/Tax_Credit" class="mw-redirect" title="Tax Credit">tax credits</a>, voting with the Government in favour of the plan. This was particularly outrageous for his critics because he flew in from abroad on his personal plane to vote, when his voting record was scant.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In October 2017 Webber retired from the House of Lords, stating that his busy schedule was incompatible with the demands of Parliament considering the upcoming crucial Brexit legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-20171016_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-20171016-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2009, Lloyd Webber had surgery for early-stage <a href="/wiki/Prostate_cancer" title="Prostate cancer">prostate cancer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lloyd_Webber_treated_for_cancer_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd_Webber_treated_for_cancer-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> but had to be readmitted to hospital with post-operative infection in November. In January 2010, he declared he was cancer-free.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> He had his prostate completely removed as a preventative measure.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours_and_styles_of_address">Honours and styles of address</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Honours and styles of address">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lloyd Webber was appointed <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">Knight Bachelor</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1992_Birthday_Honours" title="1992 Birthday Honours">1992 Birthday Honours</a> for services to the Arts.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/1997_New_Year_Honours" title="1997 New Year Honours">1997 New Year Honours</a> he was created a <a href="/wiki/Life_peer" title="Life peer">life peer</a> as <b>Baron Lloyd-Webber</b>, of Sydmonton in the <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">County of Hampshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gaz_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaz-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He is properly styled as <b>The Lord Lloyd-Webber</b>; the title is hyphenated, although his surname is not.<sup id="cite_ref-whoswho_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He sat as a Conservative member of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> until his retirement from the House on 17 October 2017.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Styles_of_address">Styles of address</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Styles of address">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>1948\xe2\x80\x931992:</b> <i>Mr</i> Andrew Lloyd Webber</li>\n<li><b>1992\xe2\x80\x931997:</b> <i>Sir</i> Andrew Lloyd Webber</li>\n<li><b>1997\xe2\x80\x93present:</b> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Right_Honourable" title="The Right Honourable">The Right Honourable</a></i> The Lord Lloyd-Webber, Kt</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academy_Awards">Academy Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Academy Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>1996</b> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a> for "<a href="/wiki/You_Must_Love_Me" title="You Must Love Me">You Must Love Me</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(1996_film)" title="Evita (1996 film)">Evita</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Evita_(1996_film)" title="List of accolades received by Evita (1996 film)">award shared</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sir_Tim_Rice" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Tim Rice">Sir Tim Rice</a>)</li></ul>\n<p>One nomination for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Academy Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Song Score and Adaptation</a>: 1973 motion picture <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar_(film)" title="Jesus Christ Superstar (film)">Jesus Christ Superstar</a></i>\n</p><p>One nomination for Best Original Song: "<a href="/wiki/Learn_to_Be_Lonely" title="Learn to Be Lonely">Learn to Be Lonely</a>" from the 2004 motion picture <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(2004_film)" title="The Phantom of the
