<i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(1996_movie)" class="mw-redirect" title="Evita (1996 movie)">Evita</a></i> (1996) was directed by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Parker" title="Alan Parker">Alan Parker</a>; and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(2004_film)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (2004 film)">The Phantom of the Opera</a></i> (2004) was directed by <a href="/wiki/Joel_Schumacher" title="Joel Schumacher">Joel Schumacher</a> and co-produced by Lloyd Webber. <i><a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">Cats</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Joseph_and_the_Amazing_Technicolor_Dreamcoat" title="Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat">Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar" title="Jesus Christ Superstar">Jesus Christ Superstar</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/By_Jeeves" title="By Jeeves">By Jeeves</a></i> have been adapted into made-for-television films that have been released on <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> and <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">VHS</a> and often air on <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>.\n</p><p>A special performance of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_at_the_Royal_Albert_Hall" title="The Phantom of the Opera at the Royal Albert Hall">The Phantom of the Opera at the Royal Albert Hall</a></i> for the 25th anniversary was broadcast live to cinemas in early October 2011 and later released on DVD and Blu-ray in February 2012. The same was also done with a reworked version of <i>Love Never Dies</i>. Filmed in <a href="/wiki/Melbourne,_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Melbourne, Australia">Melbourne, Australia</a>, it received a limited cinema release in the US and Canada in 2012, to see if it would be viable to bring the show to <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a>. It received positive reviews and was No.1 on DVD charts in the UK and Ireland, and did well in America.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_works">Other works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Odessa_File_(film)" title="The Odessa File (film)">The Odessa File</a></i> (1974) \xe2\x80\x93 Film score.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Variations_(Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_album)" title="Variations (Andrew Lloyd Webber album)">Variations</a></i> (1978) \xe2\x80\x93 A set of musical variations on <a href="/wiki/Niccol%C3%B2_Paganini" title="Niccol\xc3\xb2 Paganini">Niccol\xc3\xb2 Paganini</a>\'s Caprice in A&#160;minor that Lloyd Webber composed for his brother, cellist Julian. This album featured fifteen rock musicians including guitarist <a href="/wiki/Gary_Moore" title="Gary Moore">Gary Moore</a> and pianist <a href="/wiki/Rod_Argent" title="Rod Argent">Rod Argent</a> and reached number 2 in the UK album chart upon its release. It was later combined with <i><a href="/wiki/Tell_Me_on_a_Sunday" title="Tell Me on a Sunday">Tell Me on a Sunday</a></i> to form one show, <i><a href="/wiki/Song_and_Dance" title="Song and Dance">Song and Dance</a></i>. Lloyd Webber also used variation five as the basis for <i><a href="/wiki/Unexpected_Song" title="Unexpected Song">Unexpected Song</a></i> in Song and Dance. The main theme is used as the theme music to <i><a href="/wiki/The_South_Bank_Show" title="The South Bank Show">The South Bank Show</a></i>.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Webber)" class="mw-redirect" title="Requiem (Webber)">Requiem</a></i> (1985) \xe2\x80\x93 A classical choral work composed in honour of his father, William.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Watership_Down_(TV_series)" title="Watership Down (TV series)">Watership Down</a></i> (1999) - Lloyd Webber and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Batt" title="Mike Batt">Mike Batt</a>, main soundtrack composer of the animated series adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Watership_Down" title="Watership Down">Richard Adams\' novel of the same name</a>, composed the song "Fields of Sun". The actual song was never used on the show, nor was it available on the CD soundtrack that was released at the time. He was however still credited for the unused song in the show\'s opening titles.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andrew_Lloyd_Webber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber_discography" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber discography">Andrew Lloyd Webber discography</a></div>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Likes_of_Us" title="The Likes of Us">The Likes of Us</a></i> (1965)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Joseph_and_the_Amazing_Technicolor_Dreamcoat" title="Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat">Joseph and the Amazing Technicolor Dreamcoat</a></i> (1968)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ_Superstar" title="Jesus Christ Superstar">Jesus Christ Superstar</a></i> (1970)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/By_Jeeves" title="By Jeeves">Jeeves</a></i> (1975)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(musical)" title="Evita (musical)">Evita</a></i> (1976)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Tell_Me_On_A_Sunday" class="mw-redirect" title="Tell Me On A Sunday">Tell Me On A Sunday</a></i> (1979)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">Cats</a></i> (1981)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Song_and_Dance" title="Song and Dance">Song and Dance</a></i> (1982)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Starlight_Express" title="Starlight Express">Starlight Express</a></i> (1984)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom
